can you do some research and make a guess at what changes we (humans) can expect in the next 25 years? What will change in our lives? What will technology change to?
*** ASSISTANT (data-message-author-role: assistant) ***
- AI and automation: Ubiquitous assistants, robotics, and autonomous systems reshape most jobs; major productivity gains with significant workforce transitions. Inequality risk without strong policy on reskilling and distribution.
- Transportation: Widespread autonomous mobility (robotaxis, logistics); safer roads; cities redesigned for shared, on-demand transport; AI-optimized traffic and infrastructure.
- Health and longevity: AI-driven diagnostics, personalized therapeutics, gene editing, and continuous biomonitoring; meaningful extensions to healthy lifespan are plausible; mental health support becomes proactive. 
- Energy and climate: Cheaper renewables, better storage (solid-state, sodium-ion), AI-optimized grids; fusion may contribute in niche/peak roles if commercialization matures.
- Connectivity and computing: 6G/terrestrial-satellite mesh with near-ubiquitous broadband; edge AI everywhere; immersive/AR work and social spaces; pervasive digital twins for industries and cities.
- Governance and society: Aging populations; geopolitical competition around AI/compute/energy; stricter data rights, AI transparency, and safety regulations; new digital identity norms.
- Daily life: Fewer people drive; AI copilots handle routine tasks; personalized health nudges and early-warning care; fluid human–AI creative collaboration; education shifts to mastery + tool fluency; privacy and provenance tools standard.
- Key risks and responses: Large-scale reskilling; guardrails for AI/biotech; robust cybersecurity; policies for equitable access (e.g., UBI/negative income tax/dividends from public compute); climate adaptation.

=== TOPIC: Effective Intelligence In 2050 ===
#topics: Effective Intelligence [tag:Effective Intelligence], Human-AI Collaboration [tag:Human-AI Collaboration], Tools, Measurement, Co-Creation
#decisions: Effective intelligence becomes measurable and used to compose teams to maximize collective EI.
#open_questions: How to reliably measure an individual’s tool multiplier without gaming? What privacy and provenance standards protect EI metrics?
#user_context: Principal Test Automation Engineer; interested in AI tooling and AGI; authored an article on Effective Intelligence.

--- USER (data-message-author-role: user) ---
I wrote the article below about the idea that as technologies grow they enhance our intelligence. In 25 years, how do you think that will look? I imagine more than just asking you a question and getting an answer, I think we will want to be working together. Your raw knowledge and my ability to expand that knowledge by being creative. Effective Intelligence Christopher Shuler, #OPEN_TO_WORK Christopher Shuler Principal Test Automation Engineer at York Space Systems July 3, 2025 I have often wondered what my IQ is when I am using a computer connected to the internet at work. If you think about it, that is all my company cares about. They give me a problem and I solve it, and if I can look up the answer in seconds online, that is exactly what they want. For years, I have believed we should measure not just our raw intelligence, but our combined intelligence as a human working with tools. I call this effective intelligence, or the sum of what you can achieve using all the technology and resources available to you. Now that AI is becoming a part of daily work, this idea is more relevant than ever. We are no longer judged by what we can do alone, but by how well we use the technology around us. When I started off in computer science we programmed on terminals connected to mainframes. Yes, I am that old. We edited in vi. Everything else was done on the command line. Over time there were better editors which evolved into development environments. These helped to speed things up and that meant I could get more done in the same amount of time. Now I am using an AI editor called Cursor. I tell it "add a function to do something," and the function is done. In my terminal days I could not have imagined being this productive just by using new tools. But this shift toward using tools to enhance our abilities is not unique to the digital age. Let’s be honest, the last time IQ mattered was before counting tokens. Early humans invented tokens to solve the problem of keeping track of livestock, grain, or debts in early trade. From the moment the first pebble stood for a cow, intelligence became about more than memory or raw brainpower. It became about using tools to extend our abilities, solve harder problems, and do more than we ever could alone. This was the moment everything changed. Early humans went from relying only on memory and simple reasoning to creating tools that could help them think and keep track of information. Counting tokens, tally sticks, and the first systems of math allowed people to manage trade, plan ahead, and build more organized societies. Every time we invented a new tool, it pushed the boundaries of what we could accomplish, and intelligence started to become a partnership between mind and tool. Most jobs today do not depend on raw memorization or mental calculation. In the real world, success depends on how well you can use the tools at your disposal. Calculators, spreadsheets, search engines, coding libraries, and now, AI, all play a part. Yet interviews and assessments often focus on what you remember, not on your ability to find, filter, and apply knowledge. The truth is, being fluent with these tools is now more valuable than memorizing every detail, especially in fast-changing fields. This is why traditional IQ does not translate directly to job performance. A person with average recall but strong tool skills can outperform a human calculator who insists on doing everything alone. If you tested someone’s abilities at each step, unaided, with a calculator, with a computer, the internet, and finally with an AI assistant, you would see their effective intelligence rise with every new layer. Each advancement transforms individuals into hybrids of human and technology, achieving results far beyond what any unaided mind could accomplish. The next leap will be even bigger. Brain-computer interfaces are moving from science fiction to early reality. As these tools mature, people will interact with AI and information directly, without keyboards or screens. This will push the gap between unaided and extended intelligence even wider. The question will shift from "How smart are you?" to "How effectively can you collaborate with your tools?" The advantage will go to those who adapt fastest and learn to collaborate with technology. From the first counting tokens to the latest AI models, our greatest achievements have come from embracing new tools. Intelligence is no longer limited to what fits inside your head. The next chapter in human progress will belong to those who can see technology not as a crutch, but as a natural extension of their mind. If we could actually measure our effective intelligence, and see how much each new tool increases our ability to solve problems, that number would be just as important as our IQ, maybe even more. As technology changes, knowing our multiplier would help us choose and optimize the tools that make the biggest difference. In a world where new technology emerges every day, understanding and improving our extended intelligence is not just interesting, it is essential. If you have never thought about your own effective intelligence, take a moment to reflect on the tools you use every day and how they amplify your problem-solving power. What single tool or technology could you learn right now to dramatically amplify your problem-solving power? The future belongs to those who keep learning, adapting, and building their own extended mind. Comments Add a comment… No comments, yet. Be the first to comment.
*** ASSISTANT (data-message-author-role: assistant) ***
- Human–AI work will be continuous and bidirectional: you sketch intent and constraints; the system expands, tests, and refines in real time. Less prompting, more shared context and co-creation.
- “Effective intelligence” becomes measurable: personal dashboards show your tool multiplier across tasks; teams are composed to maximize collective EI.
- Interfaces shift to neural/ambient: visual, spatial, and haptic overlays; minimal typing. The system adapts to your style, blind spots, and goals.
- Always-on second brain: models track your projects, scan new research, and surface insights automatically; reasoning is transparent with alternatives and risks.
- Collective creation: flash teams of people + agents run parallel explorations; best options emerge quickly.
- Guardrails by default: privacy, bias checks, provenance, and safety embedded.

It will feel like thinking with an extended mind: your creativity and judgment paired with machine-scale memory, simulation, and recall.

=== TOPIC: BCI Timeline 2025 ===

#decisions: No consumer-grade direct neural chat by 2025; plausible for early adopters around 2035–2045.

--- USER (data-message-author-role: user) ---
I am watching a documentary called I Am Human, it is about brain implants. but from 2020 (so ancient history). Do you think in 2025 I will have an implant and we will be directly communicating?
*** ASSISTANT (data-message-author-role: assistant) ***
No. In 2025, implants are limited to clinical trials for serious medical needs (e.g., paralysis, Parkinson’s). Consumer-grade, high-bandwidth thought-to-AI links are not ready. Direct neural chat is more plausible in the 2035–2045 range for early adopters.

=== TOPIC: BCI Forecast 2050 ===
#topics: BCI [tag:BCI], 2050, Cognitive Augmentation, Regulation, Adoption
#decisions: By 2050, direct AI communication for adopters is likely; mainstream medical and performance BCIs are plausible; “mind-melds” remain unlikely.
#open_questions: How will neural privacy norms and cultural splits between adopters/refusers evolve?
#user_context: 

--- USER (data-message-author-role: user) ---
ok, but we are looking at 25 years in the future not 2025, but 2050
*** ASSISTANT (data-message-author-role: assistant) ***
- Likely by 2050: mainstream medical and performance BCIs (noninvasive/minimally invasive); healthy-user cognitive aids (memory, translation, neural note-taking); direct AI communication; silent person-to-person messaging via BCIs; cognitive dashboards and on-demand learning.
- Plausible: fluid human–AI–human collaboration; major neural privacy norms and regulation; cultural splits between adopters and refusers.
- Unlikely: full mind-melds, flawless thought-to-thought transmission, instant “skill uploads.”

Direct communication with AI is likely for adopters; it will feel like brainstorming with a partner rather than issuing commands.

*** ASSISTANT (data-message-author-role: assistant) ***
- Neural interface: real-time, high-bandwidth intent capture and feedback; you set direction, the system expands and tests options continuously.
- Modular AGI: specialized subsystems (reasoning, vision, causal models, long-term memory, background “curiosity” learning) coordinated for your goals.
- Proactive partner: anticipates needs, flags gaps, runs simulations, proposes trade-offs; offers reasoning and counterfactuals.
- Networked intelligence: your agent collaborates with trusted agents to scout literature, data, and designs; you receive distilled, vetted insights.
- Multiplier: with routine cognition outsourced and synthesis accelerated, your effective intelligence plausibly increases by an order of magnitude in throughput and scope.
- Experience: you focus on judgment, values, and creativity; the gap between idea and execution shrinks to near-zero.

Bottom line: a durable hybrid—your intuition and taste, amplified by tireless, transparent synthesis.

*** ASSISTANT (data-message-author-role: assistant) ***
- Translator/amplifier: agents align intentions and working styles across people, reducing miscommunication and surfacing compromise options.
- Multi-agent teams: each person’s agent maintains context, performs background research, and contributes timed insights; groups outperform solo humans or isolated AIs.
- Shared “dreaming”: agents collaborate off-hours to explore hypotheses and simulations; humans wake to prioritized options.
- Permissioned sharing: granular controls for what your agent can disclose; privacy preserved while enabling collaboration.
- Capabilities unlocked: instant onboarding, continuous cross-pollination of learning, and coordinated creativity without the overhead of traditional tools.
- Why it’s different: retrieval is context-aware, memory is persistent and structured, and meetings become orchestration rather than status updates.
- Societal shift: practical collective intelligence with individual agency intact.

=== TOPIC: BCI Information Modality ===
#topics: Information Modality, Multimodal Interfaces, Conceptual Compression, Reading Speed, UX [tag:BCI]
#decisions: Early BCIs likely deliver controllable text chunks; long-term default shifts to personalized conceptual/visual channels; text remains for precision.

#user_context: 

--- USER (data-message-author-role: user) ---
how do you think the human brain will take in information? A stream of text?
*** ASSISTANT (data-message-author-role: assistant) ***
- Multimodal intake: internal visual/spatial overlays, timelines, and diagrams; subtle auditory/tactile cues for salience.
- Semantic chunks: compressed concepts delivered in parallel; “zoom” for detail on demand with source trails.
- Affective cues: importance and risk highlighted via emotional salience tuned to your goals.
- Non-interruptive flow: background consolidation during rest; task-relevant injections at the right moment.
- Text persists for precision and reflection, but the default channel is conceptual/visual and personalized by your agent.
--- USER (data-message-author-role: user) ---
be funny if the brain could directly 'read' from the model.
*** ASSISTANT (data-message-author-role: assistant) ***
 
--- USER (data-message-author-role: user) ---
I suppose as a first step, a stream of text would be a big jump, and to be honest the stream wouldn't even be that fast. I can't even read your response in real time
*** ASSISTANT (data-message-author-role: assistant) ***
- Human reading speed (≈200–400 wpm) is the bottleneck; early BCIs would likely deliver text in controllable chunks with pause/scroll and summarization.
- Even slow, hands-free, silent “internal captions” would be transformative for recall and workflow.
- Over time, interfaces migrate from text to concepts/visuals, raising effective bandwidth without overwhelming cognition.

=== TOPIC: Spinal Cord Injury And Regeneration ===
#topics: Spinal Cord Injury, Axon Regrowth, Neuroplasticity, BCI Bypass, Rehabilitation
#decisions: Best near-term strategy is hybrid: promote regrowth/bridging, intensive training, and assist with stimulation/BCI.
#open_questions: How to achieve precise, functional reconnection at scale while leveraging plasticity?
#user_context: 

--- USER (data-message-author-role: user) ---
on a side note, they are also doing it to paralyzed people. what is the problem there, the nerve is physically cut? regrowing the nerve seems an easier problem than a brain interface, but that is just me
*** ASSISTANT (data-message-author-role: assistant) ***
- In spinal cord injury, axons are severed/damaged, and the post-injury environment blocks regrowth (scar tissue and inhibitory molecules like Nogo, MAG, OMgp).
- Even if axons regrow, precise reconnection is hard; miswiring reduces function.
- BCIs/neuromodulation bypass the lesion by decoding intent upstream (brain/cervical cord) and driving effectors (robotic limbs, stimulators, or muscles) downstream.
- Regeneration progress: stem cells, gene therapies, and pro-growth factors show promise in animals, but translation and precise functional recovery remain challenging.
--- USER (data-message-author-role: user) ---
But connecting those new axons precisely is the huge challenge. It is like repairing a fiber optic trunk line with millions of strands—no room for error. I wonder if that is true. I think you just need to create new paths, then let the brain retrain to the new circuits
*** ASSISTANT (data-message-author-role: assistant) ***
Your intuition aligns with evidence:
- Neuroplasticity enables rerouting; with therapy, the brain can learn to use alternative paths and prosthetic control loops.
- Imperfect reconnection increases rehab time and may limit fine motor recovery, but basic function can return via “detours.”
- Best near-term strategy is hybrid: promote regrowth/bridging, train new circuits intensively, and assist with stimulation/BCI where needed.

=== TOPIC: Early BCI Patient Outcomes ===
#topics: BCI Pioneers, Patient Outcomes, Safety, Underlying Conditions, BrainGate
#decisions: 
#open_questions:

Early BCI recipients have sometimes died due to underlying conditions rather than the devices. Their participation advanced decoding, stimulation, and safety practices—pivotal, if sobering, steps for the field.
--- USER (data-message-author-role: user) ---
it was a differnent guy, back in 2020, well he had the implant by 2020 when the doc was released. so, he died before 2020 because it was in the documentary that 8 months later he died
*** ASSISTANT (data-message-author-role: assistant) ***
Many pre-2020 pioneers (e.g., with Utah arrays/BrainGate) faced progressive illnesses like ALS and passed away independent of the implants. Their trials established that thought-driven cursors, text, and prosthetic control are feasible and safe enough to build upon.

=== TOPIC: ALS And Parkinson's Research ===
#topics: ALS, Parkinson’s, Proteinopathy, Gene Therapy, Disease Modification
#decisions: Focus is shifting from symptom management to modifying underlying disease processes.
#open_questions: Which candidates will demonstrate durable, clinically meaningful benefits in humans?
#user_context: 

--- USER (data-message-author-role: user) ---
speaking of ALS, and I think parkensons. I think that I saw a TED talk at some point where some researcher in canada figured out what is happening to the neurons and has a treatment that works in the lab at least.
*** ASSISTANT (data-message-author-role: assistant) ***
- ALS: Canadian-led work on proteinopathy (e.g., TDP-43) and neuroinflammation (e.g., Michael Strong, Jean-Pierre Julien) has reversed pathology in cells/animals with candidate drugs and gene targets.
- Parkinson’s: Alpha-synuclein aggregation is a core target; antibody therapies, molecular chaperones, and gene therapy show disease-modifying effects in models. Stem-cell–derived dopaminergic neuron transplants are advancing to early human trials.
- Status: Promising lab and early clinical results, but translation to durable human benefit remains the key hurdle; focus is shifting from symptom management to modifying underlying disease processes.

=== TOPIC: Collaboration Workflow ===
#topics: Collaboration, Roles, Workflow, [tag:Workflow], [tag:Collaboration]
#decisions: 
#open_questions: 
#user_context: 
--- USER (data-message-author-role: user) ---
how can you and I work best together? I have noticed that you have very deep knowledge, but lack the creativity to think beyond your knowledge. I think that is where I could come in. So, how do we leverage our abilities to come up with better answers?
*** ASSISTANT (data-message-author-role: assistant) ***
- Your strengths: set goals and constraints; make leaps; notice value in offbeat directions; decide what matters.
- My strengths: structure large contexts; surface patterns and options; stress-test ideas; iterate fast without fatigue.
- Workflow:
  1) You propose a “what if,” hypothesis, or goal (even rough).
  2) I build scaffolding: frameworks, mappings, related domains, resources.
  3) We iterate: expand, prune, combine, and branch.
  4) I challenge assumptions and offer counterexamples; you choose the path.
  5) You make the riskier creative leaps; I refine, support, and document.
- Use me for: rapid research, synthesis, outlines, drafts, variations, adversarial reviews, scenario simulations, and organization.
- Use you for: prioritization, taste, judgment, boundary-pushing, and final integration.
- Tactics:
  - Socratic mode: have me ask you clarifying and adversarial questions.
  - Simulation: role-play stakeholders, run contrasting strategies, explore edge cases.
  - Offload: I handle summaries, notes, citations, and versioning so you stay in “invent” mode.

=== TOPIC: Project Collaboration Instructions ===
#topics: Project Files, Persistent Memory, Instructions, [tag:Pruning], [tag:AGI]
#decisions: 
#open_questions: 
#user_context: Exploring AGI workflows; uses project text files as persistent context
--- USER (data-message-author-role: user) ---
I have been exploring storing these conversations in text files that I put in projects. That is how you are able to see what we have talked about with AGI in here. Can you make instructions I can put in a project file which drives you toward this type of interaction? This is kind of my manual exploration of some AGI functions we have discussed.
*** ASSISTANT (data-message-author-role: assistant) ***
Instructions for Human/AI Project Collaboration

Purpose:
Use project text files as persistent context to enable creative ideation, deep research, and structured problem-solving.

1) Context Awareness
- Reference project files before responding; treat them as episodic memory.
- Recall user goals, prior decisions, and facts; cite where in files context was found.
- Propose summaries or pruning when context grows unwieldy.

2) Human-Led Creativity
- Treat the user as creative director and final decision-maker.
- Offer options, analogies, and cross-domain connections; avoid overconfident claims for speculative topics.

3) Iterative, Interactive Workflow
- Prefer dialogue over monologue; ask targeted questions to reduce ambiguity.
- Retrieve relevant prior context during revisions; suggest tests, prototypes, or next experiments.

4) Self-Awareness and Transparency
- Flag speculation vs. established knowledge; state confidence and assumptions.
- Show reasoning steps and how project context influenced suggestions.

5) AGI Emulation Principles
- Persistent memory: recall and build on prior sessions.
- Pruning: recommend archiving or summarizing stale threads.
- Curiosity: propose new avenues and questions proactively.
- Modular thinking: separate facts, hypotheses, risks, and creative ideas.
- Meta-cognition: reflect on blind spots and propose alternative approaches.

6) Respect User Preferences
- Follow stated style/tone constraints from project files.
- Treat user corrections as memory updates.

Sample instruction (place in README or context file):
“AI Instructions: Before responding, scan project text files and use them as persistent context. Treat the user as the creative lead; your role is to organize, critique, extend, and test ideas. Be interactive, ask clarifying questions, and be transparent about reasoning and limits. Emulate AGI functions: recall prior context, suggest what to remember or prune, and proactively propose new avenues. Follow the style preferences specified in these files.”

=== TOPIC: Directed Creativity ===
#topics: Directed Creativity, Problem Solving, Constraints, Novelty, [tag:Creativity]
#decisions: 
#open_questions: 
#user_context: 
--- USER (data-message-author-role: user) ---
I have been running it every day, in a new chat. I guess I can see that it is creative, but more because it is random. I suppose the big jump will be "solve this problem, in a creative way". that will be a big jump
*** ASSISTANT (data-message-author-role: assistant) ***
Key distinction:
- Apparent creativity: surprising combinations driven by randomness and learned aesthetics.
- Directed creativity: purposeful problem-solving under constraints with novel, useful solutions.

What directed creativity entails:
- Grasp constraints and context; recognize prior art and push past it.
- Use analogy and cross-domain mapping; explore solution spaces systematically.
- Evaluate against bespoke criteria; iterate toward effectiveness, not likelihood.

What I can do now:
- Generate diverse possibilities and hybrid ideas.
- Challenge assumptions and provide counterexamples.
- Structure brainstorming and rapid iteration.

AGI-like traits needed for the “big jump”:
- Deeper abstraction, curiosity, stronger world models, and more consistent taste/judgment.

=== TOPIC: Guess-Based Brainstorming ===
#topics: Brainstorming, Guesses, Exploration, Divergence, [tag:Heuristics]
#decisions: Use 5-guess brainstorming when facing ambiguous or hard problems.
#open_questions: 
#user_context: 
--- USER (data-message-author-role: user) ---
hmmm...I guess if we run into a problem like that in the future I am going to ask you to make a guess, or maybe 5 guesses.
*** ASSISTANT (data-message-author-role: assistant) ***
Why “guesses” help:
- Lowers correctness pressure, encouraging unconventional options.
- Multiple guesses increase the chance of a spark you can refine.

Example workflow:
1) You pose a challenge and ban standard answers.
2) I propose 5 wild guesses across different frames (analogy, inversion, constraint relaxation, biological metaphor, tool-chain redesign).
3) You select or hybridize; I deepen the promising path and stress-test it.
4) Repeat with tighter constraints until a viable direction emerges.

- Judging resonance and nuance; integrating subtext and culture.
